\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\subsubsection*{template$<$typename Derived$>$\newline
class Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base$<$ Derived $>$}
\doxylink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOpImpl}{Base} class for all 1D and 2D array, and related expressions. 

An array is similar to a dense vector or matrix. While matrices are mathematical objects with well defined linear algebra operators, an array is just a collection of scalar values arranged in a one or two dimensionnal fashion. As the main consequence, all operations applied to an array are performed coefficient wise. Furthermore, arrays support scalar math functions of the c++ standard library (e.\+g., std\+::sin(x)), and convenient constructors allowing to easily write generic code working for both scalar values and arrays.

This class is the base that is inherited by all array expression types.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Derived} & is the derived type, e.\+g., an array or an expression type.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
This class can be extended with the help of the plugin mechanism described on the page Topic\+Customizing\+\_\+\+Plugins by defining the preprocessor symbol {\ttfamily EIGEN\+\_\+\+ARRAYBASE\+\_\+\+PLUGIN}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}, Topic\+Class\+Hierarchy 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{DoxyReturn}
The template parameter {\itshape Custom\+Binary\+Op} is the type of the functor of the custom operator (see class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Cwise\+Binary\+Op} for an example)

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_aae5d1acb616f0c1f6052c3383574471c}\index{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}!cwiseEqual@{cwiseEqual}}
\index{cwiseEqual@{cwiseEqual}!Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{cwiseEqual()}{cwiseEqual()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_aae5d1acb616f0c1f6052c3383574471c} 
template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived$>$ \\
EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1numext_1_1equal__to}{numext\+::equal\+\_\+to}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_a5feed465b3a8e60c47e73ecce83e39a2}{Scalar}} $>$, const Derived, const Other\+Derived $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::cwise\+Equal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const EIGEN\+\_\+\+CURRENT\+\_\+\+STORAGE\+\_\+\+BASE\+\_\+\+CLASS$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise == operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than().
\end{DoxyWarning}
Example\+: 
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}{0}

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\+: 
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_a27bfdb32677ef8e25b1d2302a25ea504}\index{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}!cwiseEqual@{cwiseEqual}}
\index{cwiseEqual@{cwiseEqual}!Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{cwiseEqual()}{cwiseEqual()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_a27bfdb32677ef8e25b1d2302a25ea504} 
template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Cwise\+Scalar\+Equal\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::cwise\+Equal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_a5feed465b3a8e60c47e73ecce83e39a2}{Scalar}} \&}]{s}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise == operator of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and a scalar {\itshape s} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than().
\end{DoxyWarning}

\index{cwiseNotEqual@{cwiseNotEqual}!Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{cwiseNotEqual()}{cwiseNotEqual()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_ac56a786746ba8323eae9bfdd735c6f06} 
template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived$>$ \\
EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1numext_1_1not__equal__to}{numext\+::not\+\_\+equal\+\_\+to}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_a5feed465b3a8e60c47e73ecce83e39a2}{Scalar}} $>$, const Derived, const Other\+Derived $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::cwise\+Not\+Equal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const EIGEN\+\_\+\+CURRENT\+\_\+\+STORAGE\+\_\+\+BASE\+\_\+\+CLASS$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise != operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than().
\end{DoxyWarning}

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}

\end{DoxyVerbInclude}

\index{expm1@{expm1}!Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{expm1()}{expm1()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_a2653aab701b99d90f161f36e6581bbe7} 
template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseUnaryOp}{Expm1\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::expm1 (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise exponential of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this minus 1.
\end{DoxyReturn}
In exact arithmetic, {\ttfamily x.\+expm1()} is equivalent to {\ttfamily x.\+exp()} -\/ 1, however, with finite precision, this function is much more accurate when {\ttfamily x} is close to zero.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_a438640146f3e7488f09a4f60c305b1d9} 
template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseUnaryOp}{Log1p\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::log1p (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise logarithm of 1 plus {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
In exact arithmetic, {\ttfamily x.\+log()} is equivalent to {\ttfamily }(x+1).\doxylink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_a7748ba1f6891fa4e10723a8bf77b8770}{log()}, however, with finite precision, this function is much more accurate when {\ttfamily x} is close to zero.

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_ac2bbbcf6db4b01cea5caeb5aadb4b1d8}\index{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}!ndtri@{ndtri}}
\index{ndtri@{ndtri}!Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ndtri()}{ndtri()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_ac2bbbcf6db4b01cea5caeb5aadb4b1d8} 
template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseUnaryOp}{Ndtri\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::ndtri (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise inverse of the CDF of the Normal distribution function function of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\textbackslash{}specialfunctions\+\_\+module

In other words, considering {\ttfamily x = ndtri(y)}, it returns the argument, x, for which the area under the Gaussian probability density function (integrated from minus infinity to x) is equal to y.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function supports only float and double scalar types. To support other scalar types, the user has to provide implementations of ndtri(\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\href{group__CoeffwiseMathFunctions.html\#cwisetable_ndtri}{\texttt{Math functions}} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived$>$ \\
EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC Derived \& \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase}{Eigen\+::\+Dense\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::operator= (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1EigenBase}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Copies the generic expression {\itshape other} into \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this. 

The expression must provide a (templated) eval\+To(\+Derived\& dst) const function which does the actual job. In practice, this allows any user to write its own special matrix without having to modify \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}

a reference to \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than().
\end{DoxyWarning}

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}

In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than().

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_ad996aade2210f810f1b11d43a611b1e3}\index{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}!zeta@{zeta}}
\index{zeta@{zeta}!Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::ArrayBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{zeta()}{zeta()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase_ad996aade2210f810f1b11d43a611b1e3} 
template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
template$<$typename DerivedQ$>$ \\
const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__zeta__op}{internal\+::scalar\+\_\+zeta\+\_\+op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_a5feed465b3a8e60c47e73ecce83e39a2}{Scalar}} $>$, const Derived, const DerivedQ $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1ArrayBase}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::zeta (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const EIGEN\+\_\+\+CURRENT\+\_\+\+STORAGE\+\_\+\+BASE\+\_\+\+CLASS$<$ DerivedQ $>$ \&}]{q}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise zeta function.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\textbackslash{}specialfunctions\+\_\+module

It returns the Riemann zeta function of two arguments {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and {\itshape q\+:} 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em q} & is the shift, it must be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 0\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this is the exponent, it must be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 1. 

This function supports only float and double scalar types. To support other scalar types, the user has to provide implementations of zeta(\+T,\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}
This method is an alias for zeta(\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this,q);

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
Eigen\+::zeta() 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise power of the scalar {\itshape x} to the given array of {\itshape exponents}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
This function computes the coefficient-\/wise power between a scalar and an array of exponents.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_a5feed465b3a8e60c47e73ecce83e39a2}{Scalar}} & is the scalar type of {\itshape x}. It must be compatible with the scalar type of the given array expression ({\ttfamily Derived\+::\+Scalar}).\\
